< Review>
Reading reviews online and believing them has bitten me more than once.

The short review: The pizza is decent

The long review:  I walked in to order.  The man must have been having a bad day, he didn't look like he wanted to be there.  Who would...it is 100 degrees outside and they have no air conditioning inside...what's up with that?

I place my order and tell him that I really like mushrooms and asked if I should order extra mushrooms to make sure i get my fill of them...he said "no, we put plenty on, you'll like it.  If you don't, order more next time".  I said Okay and paid for the pizza.

As I walked over to sit down to wait for the pizza (sweating) a cockroach crawls across the floor, in broad daylight!  I've seen some roaches in my time, and they don't like to come out in the day time unless they are very comfortable doing so.   Given the location of the restaurant, roaches do not seem out of place.

The rest of the place seemed clean, but when I got my pizza, it smelled good and i took it to the hotel.  When I opened the box, I was a bit disappointed in the number of mushrooms...should have ordered extra :(

For what it's worth, I won't get pizza there again while I'm going to be here in the area.  It was better than the cheap joints, not the best I've had though.< /Review>

Pinecrest Campground is a wonderful place to swim, sail and to hike around one of the most beautiful lakes in California. If you have asthma, please be careful due to the poor air quality. Right now it is the smoke, from the fires, that is the problem. Over the last five years, I have had severe asthma attacks from the campfire smoke that hovers above the campground. If you don‚Äôt have asthma or a compromised immune system then you will be fine.<//text>

<rating>5<//rating>< review>
Pinecrest campground has been our spot for 15 yrs now, we go once a year and stay for at least 5days, anything shorter is depriving your inner child of playtime. The sites are always clean at check in and the restrooms are maintained accordingly, be sure to report any unruly guests, we had too last time just to keep it clean, kids were having a wet toilet paper war in one of the RR. Remember you can't control the weather and you can't pick your neighbors, so enjoy the stay as best you can, do your research on peak visit/camping days, weather/ fire/road conditions. Check the website for rules and regulations. Cheers.</review>

< date>

<user>101004273531868284424</user><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMxd8SqKEixUuFypix6IzWq9e4Hwa-G7LtQKsHN=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNYlDqf7ocvrOyhahGJy7YmYZ8kFzeWqJBR_i-u=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNvE-QB1re9dqf4kwh9TWjGBCZQnYUf3uOFNvvI=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pictures><username>ryan pascoe< /username><rating>5<//rating>< review>
Pinecrest is great. Hiking around the lake takes about 2 hours. You can venture further up the mountain to Cleo's bath, where the snow run of feeds the lake. There's a good beach/swim area. Boats can be rented for cruising around. It's also great that there is a speed limit, so no wake boarding or water skiing keeps wakes and traffic low. Outdoor movie night is fun, ice cream from the store is a nightly ritual. Items at the store are a little expensive, but it's the only store for miles..... supply and demand....

Yes, this place is POPULAR, and during peak season is nearly impossible to get into last minute. You are allowed 2 vehicles and 2 tents per site, or 1 vehicle, 1 tent and a camper. With no more that 6 people per site. The reason it can seem over crowded is due to the HUGE tents, extra vehicles, and extra stuff that people bring. Certain sites are huge and can acomodate large tents, barbecues, multiple pop up canopy etc. Other sites are more confined and would be best for a couple do tents and 2 suv's. Leave your long bed deseil truck at home unless you get a site that can accommodate it! Book in advance, and ask how big the site is!</review>

<gmapID>0x8097483df59ccac9:0x828f7de149bc8193<//gmapID><Name>Ari Lehman</Name><Date>1496020522274< /Date><UserId.>109337180343199495740<//UserId.><rate>3< /rate><review>We heard all about this campsite and wanted to give a try. For us it was a two year wait, last year we had to cancel our campsite booking due to bad weather. This year we finally made the trip during the 2017 memorial weekend. Yes, you do have to book these campsites at least 6 months in advance. There is no debate the lake area is really lovely and has some nice features with a general store complex, snack bar, movie theatre, beach access, boating and hiking options. However the other reviewers are correct about the crowds, lack of parking, close campsites, the rough campsite bathrooms (no showers), and the high noise levels. This is like camping in Yosemite at the height of summer in the fraction of the space. We recommend camping outside of the valley, staying in a remote cabin and just coming in for the day (6am-10pm for day parking). We are veteran campers and for us the night time noise was intense. We had at least three large groups in our area doing heavy partying with live music plus the sounds of the nearby open air movie theatre (D loop). We ended up leaving a day early just so we could get some rest, take a shower and escape from the noise. We would definitely come back in the future but we plan on sleeping elsewhere.</review>< Resp>

<userid>105517435436896919576</userid>< gmapID>
0x8097483df59ccac9:0x828f7de149bc8193</gmapID>
<Rating>2</Rating>< Review>
The D loop of campsites was a bust for us.  The campsites are very densely packed and you end up feeling like you're right on top of other campers.  There's also little to no grass, and thus very dusty so be prepared for that.  Also, while it's nice to be so close to the lake in that you can walk to it that also means you're that much closer to the daytime hordes of people who come to hang out on the lakefront, particularly on weekends.  Some of these people see no problem in setting up their beach chairs and umbrellas right at the water's edge so that you are forced to literally walk through their stuff to actually get into the water.  The nicest part was being able to rent a 2-person kayak to go out on the lake and get away from the crowds for at least a little while.  The lake itself is certainly quite beautiful, so it's got that going for it.  Perhaps one of the other campsite loops (A, B, or C) would have been better, but I can definitely recommend avoiding loop D.</Review>

<rating>5</rating>< Text>
Great campground! So many pinetrees, great protection from the sun and wind. There is a general store that has absolutely EVERYTHING YOU NEED which is great if you forget an item or if a part in your RV breaks but, everything is super expensive at least double what you would pay at your local store. There is a restaurant, I didn't visit. And an amphitheater. The restrooms next to the amphitheater are airconditioned and automatic everything which is really nice. As for the other bathrooms they were clean, always had toilet paper, had mirrors, and not too many bugs. The lake is beautiful! The view of the mountains is breathtaking. The water was super cold but the kids didn't mind. The campsites come with one table, one firepit, and parking for two vehicles.<//Text>

< Text>
One of my favorite places to go camping! If you love camping as much as I do, then you're constantly trying to get your skeptical friends (who have never gone camping and are scared of the idea to) to come with.

This is the best place to take new campers and then anyone who loves to swim in a lake. The water here can feel cold but it's not nearly as cold as Lake Tahoe. The campsites are not too crowded and everyone is really friendly. Facilites are cleaned frequently too which is nice.

Favorite Activities/Features of Pinecrest:
- Tent camping
- Outdoor movie theatre
- Boat/kayak/canoe rental
- Swimming
- Hiking
- Restaurant
- Grocery store< /Text>

< Text>
This is a great Aquatic place.   It has Children splash area, a toddler water feature structure/ Slides, a warmer large instructional pool, and a separate training pool.  Finally it has two muti-story slides for 48" and larger people.  One is fast and other has more curves.

Fairly packed on weekends, and Summer early days.  Food onsite, Cabana rentals, and party rentals.  Pinic area, which are hard to get.   No BBQ area, but you can order BBQ items from thier menu.  All chairs, pinic area, and grass area are a first come first get.

The Life guards seem to be good and attentive.  Always could be better, but a good place to let your kids escape the hot days of Summer!< /Text>

< review>
Plenty of attentive lifeguards & areas for small kids, big kids, & adults. I wish there was more shaded seating, but my 2-year-old son loved exploring all of the water features so we didn't spend much time out of the water! & the water wasn't too warm or too cold üòé

If you want to lock up your stuff in one of the lockers instead of leaving it sit somewhere, you'll need to bring your own lock or buy one there for $5.
You can bring in snacks & baby food, but no glass containers or hard coolers. They also have food you can purchase (like a $6 burger üçî, $5 nachos, $3 corn dog, $2.75 soda, $1 bottled water, $1-3.50 ice cream, etc.).

Kids under 4 have to wear a disposable swim diaper (available to purchase there for $2) & a reusable swim diaper/liner (available for $4) under their swimsuit.

Overall, good, cool, safe fun for kiddo + mom & auntie! üòÅ

Admission without a membership is as follows (resident/non-resident):
Under 2 years = free
2-11 years = $7/$11
12-17 years = $9/$13
18+ years = $12/$16< /review>

< text>
I would like to say thank you to our server, Samantha and Bernadette.  Both ladies were super friendly, courteous and helpful.

I took my honey to celebrate his birthday at the Continental.   The menu for lunch is great.  You can have appetizers, sandwiches or lunch entrees.

Honey had a lamb sandwich with onion rings.  This lunch was $11.  I had the prime rib with potatoe salad, veggies and clam chowder.  There are other selections to pick from.

The prime rib ($15) and clam chowder was great.   They also have chicken, salmon, ribeye steak.

They have a main dinner room and a banquet room besides the bar area.   You can enjoy the dining in the bar side too.

Fridays and Saturdays, they have live bands so it gets crowded.

I highly recommend this place for lunch or dinner.   Thank you Samantha and Bernadette for making our dining experience wonderful.<//text>

<rate>5< /rate>< Review>
I stayed away from this restaurant for years, and I really regret that now. The food is delicious and the drinks are AMAZING. I got a prime rib and let me tell you, it was great. It might not be the best I've had, but I'm also comparing it to a much more expensive steak. For the price, you really really can't beat it. And the drinks were stiff.

The staff was very friendly and I have no complaints. They offered to make my very strong drink weaker, but there was no way I was going to let them do that.

The environment and ambiance itself was nice. It's dark and it is reminiscent of an old school bar. But don't let that deter you, it's a great place to go. The booths are comfortable and the music was good.

Overall, this is a great place to go. I'd highly recommend it.<//Review>

What the TV commercial doesn't say is you have to mail in a rebate form after paying full price in the store which loosely translates into you can forget about the rebate which they'll lose or deny.... Not falling for that trick again Home Depot.  If you want a basic paint color go to HD Supply, they have very limited basic colors but it's almost half the price.< /text>
